<td class="noprint" colspan="2" style="text-align:center"><img alt="" data-file-height="60" data-file-width="60" height="33" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ce/Soccerball_current_event.svg/33px-Soccerball_current_event.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ce/Soccerball_current_event.svg/50px-Soccerball_current_event.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ce/Soccerball_current_event.svg/66px-Soccerball_current_event.svg.png 2x" width="33"/> <i><a href="/wiki/2016%E2%80%9317_Swansea_City_A.F.C._season" title="2016–17 Swansea City A.F.C. season">Current season</a></i></td>

<p><b>Swansea City Association Football Club</b> (<a href="/wiki/Welsh_language" title="Welsh language">Welsh</a>: <span lang="cy" xml:lang="cy"><i>Clwb Pêl-droed Dinas Abertawe</i></span>) is a Welsh professional <a href="/wiki/Association_football" title="Association football">football</a> club based in <a href="/wiki/Swansea" title="Swansea">Swansea</a>, Wales, that plays in the <a href="/wiki/Premier_League" title="Premier League">Premier League</a>, the highest level of English football. Swansea City represent England when playing in European competitions, although they have represented Wales in the past. The club was founded in 1912 as <b>Swansea Town</b> and joined the Football League in 1921. The club changed their name in 1969, when they adopted the name <b>Swansea City</b> to reflect Swansea's new status as a <a href="/wiki/City_status_in_the_United_Kingdom" title="City status in the United Kingdom">city</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-3"><a href="#cite_note-3">[3]</a></sup> Swansea have played their home matches at the <a href="/wiki/Liberty_Stadium" title="Liberty Stadium">Liberty Stadium</a> since 2005, having previously played at the <a href="/wiki/Vetch_Field" title="Vetch Field">Vetch Field</a> since the club was founded.</p>
<p>In <a href="/wiki/1980%E2%80%9381_in_English_football" title="1980–81 in English football">1981</a>, the club was promoted to the original <a href="/wiki/Football_League_First_Division" title="Football League First Division">Football League First Division</a>. It was during the following season they came close to winning the league title, but a decline then set near the season's end before finishing sixth, although a club record. It was from here the club suffered a relegation the season after, returning to the <a href="/wiki/Football_League_Fourth_Division" title="Football League Fourth Division">Football League Fourth Division</a> a few seasons later, then narrowly avoided relegation to the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Football_Conference" title="Football Conference">Football Conference</a> in <a href="/wiki/2002%E2%80%9303_Swansea_City_A.F.C._season" title="2002–03 Swansea City A.F.C. season">2003</a>. The <a class="external text" href="http://www.swanstrust.co.uk" rel="nofollow">Swansea City Supporters Society Ltd</a> owns 20% of the club,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-4"><a href="#cite_note-4">[4]</a></sup> with their involvement hailed by <a href="/wiki/Supporters_Direct" title="Supporters Direct">Supporters Direct</a> as "the most high profile example of the involvement of a supporters' trust in the direct running of a club".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-5"><a href="#cite_note-5">[5]</a></sup> The club's subsequent climb from the fourth division of English football to the top division is chronicled in the 2014 film, <i><a href="/wiki/Jack_to_a_King_%E2%80%93_The_Swansea_Story" title="Jack to a King – The Swansea Story">Jack to a King – The Swansea Story</a></i>.</p>
<p>In 2011, Swansea were promoted to the <a href="/wiki/Premier_League" title="Premier League">Premier League</a>. On 24 February 2013, Swansea beat <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bradford_City" title="Bradford City">Bradford City</a> <a href="/wiki/2013_Football_League_Cup_Final" title="2013 Football League Cup Final">5–0</a> to win the <a href="/wiki/2012%E2%80%9313_Football_League_Cup" title="2012–13 Football League Cup">2012–13 Football League Cup</a> (the competition's highest ever winning margin for the final), winning the first major trophy in the club's history and qualifying for the <a href="/wiki/2013%E2%80%9314_UEFA_Europa_League" title="2013–14 UEFA Europa League">2013–14 UEFA Europa League</a>, where they reached the Last 32 stage but lost over two legs to <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/SSC_Napoli" title="SSC Napoli">SSC Napoli</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-6"><a href="#cite_note-6">[6]</a></sup></p>
<p></p>

<p></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Swansea_City_A.F.C.&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<dl>
<dd>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">For a statistical breakdown by season, see <a href="/wiki/List_of_Swansea_City_A.F.C._seasons" title="List of Swansea City A.F.C. seasons">List of Swansea City A.F.C. seasons</a>.</div>
</dd>
</dl>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Early_years_.281912.E2.80.931945.29">Early years (1912–1945)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Swansea_City_A.F.C.&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Early years (1912–1945)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Swansea_Town_AFC_1912-13_Squad_Photo.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="261" data-file-width="464" height="169" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6e/Swansea_Town_AFC_1912-13_Squad_Photo.jpg/300px-Swansea_Town_AFC_1912-13_Squad_Photo.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6e/Swansea_Town_AFC_1912-13_Squad_Photo.jpg/450px-Swansea_Town_AFC_1912-13_Squad_Photo.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/6/6e/Swansea_Town_AFC_1912-13_Squad_Photo.jpg 2x" width="300"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Swansea_Town_AFC_1912-13_Squad_Photo.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The Swansea Town team during its first season, 1912–13</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The area around Swansea traditionally had been a <a href="/wiki/Rugby_football" title="Rugby football">rugby</a> area, and despite previous attempts by a football club named Swansea Villa, there were no notable football clubs until the establishment of Swansea Town AFC in the summer of 1912. Following the lead of many other <a href="/wiki/South_Wales" title="South Wales">South Wales</a> sides, joined the second division of the <a href="/wiki/Southern_Football_League" title="Southern Football League">Southern League</a> for the following season. J. W. Thorpe was the club's first chairman. A site owned by Swansea Gaslight Co., called <a href="/wiki/Vetch_Field" title="Vetch Field">Vetch Field</a> due to the vegetables that grew there, was rented to be the club's ground.</p>
<p>The club's first professional match was a 1–1 draw at the Vetch Field against <a href="/wiki/Cardiff_City_F.C." title="Cardiff City F.C.">Cardiff City</a> on 7 September 1912. During that first season the <a href="/wiki/Welsh_Cup" title="Welsh Cup">Welsh Cup</a> was won for the first time, and the following season the Swans became the first side to reach the First Round of the <a href="/wiki/FA_Cup" title="FA Cup">FA Cup</a>. <a href="/wiki/Blackburn_Rovers_F.C." title="Blackburn Rovers F.C.">Blackburn Rovers</a> were the first First Division side to the visit Vetch Field for a competitive game in the 1914–1915 FA Cup – Blackburn Rovers were then the Champions of England, but Swansea Town from the Second Division of the Southern League beat them 1–0 at Vetch Field, Swansea's goal coming from <a href="/wiki/Ben_Beynon" title="Ben Beynon">Ben Beynon</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-7"><a href="#cite_note-7">[7]</a></sup> while Blackburn Rovers' penalty taker Bradshaw missed a penalty. Before the game Bradshaw had scored with thirty-six consecutive spot kicks. Remarkably, the Swans played most of the second half with ten men and the final 15 minutes with just nine men as two players were forced to retire through injury.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-8"><a href="#cite_note-8">[8]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-9"><a href="#cite_note-9">[9]</a></sup> The Swans drew at another First Division side, <a href="/wiki/Newcastle_United_F.C." title="Newcastle United F.C.">Newcastle United</a>, in the next round, before losing narrowly in the replay.</p>
<p>Following the <a href="/wiki/World_War_I" title="World War I">First World War</a> the Southern League dropped its second division, and with many clubs dropping out due to financial difficulties, the Swans were placed in the first division. After just four seasons in the Southern League, Swansea Town became founder members of the new <a href="/wiki/Football_League_Third_Division" title="Football League Third Division">Third Division</a> of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/The_Football_League" title="The Football League">The Football League</a> in 1920 and then <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Division_Three_(South)" title="Division Three (South)">Division Three (South)</a> the following season.</p>
<p>After five seasons in Division Three (South) and a few failed bids for promotion, the Swans reached the <a href="/wiki/Football_League_Second_Division" title="Football League Second Division">Second Division</a> for the first time in 1925, beating <a href="/wiki/Exeter_City_F.C." title="Exeter City F.C.">Exeter City</a> 2–1 at home on the final day of the season to beat perennial runners-up <a href="/wiki/Plymouth_Argyle_F.C." title="Plymouth Argyle F.C.">Plymouth Argyle</a> to the Championship. The side had remained unbeaten at home in the league all season – something the next promotion team would emulate over twenty years later. The following season the Swans reached the semi-finals of the FA Cup for the first time, beating Exeter City, <a href="/wiki/Watford_F.C." title="Watford F.C.">Watford</a>, <a href="/wiki/Blackpool_F.C." title="Blackpool F.C.">Blackpool</a>, Stoke City, <a href="/wiki/Millwall_F.C." title="Millwall F.C.">Millwall</a> and <a href="/wiki/Arsenal_F.C." title="Arsenal F.C.">Arsenal</a> on the way to playing the <a href="/wiki/Bolton_Wanderers_F.C." title="Bolton Wanderers F.C.">Bolton Wanderers</a> at <a href="/wiki/White_Hart_Lane" title="White Hart Lane">White Hart Lane</a>. Sadly for the Swans, an experienced Bolton side won the game 3–0 and went on to win the cup. Swans record their highest average attendance during the season of 16,118 for pre-war league games. During the 1926–27 season they beat Real Madrid 3–0 on tour and reached the FA Cup quarter-finals before losing 3–1 to Reading at the Vetch Field.</p>
<p>During the 1931–32 season they finished 1st and went out in the 3rd round of the FA Cup. However they won the Welsh Cup after beating <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Wrexham_F.C." title="Wrexham F.C.">Wrexham</a> 2–0 away after a replay, Cyril Pearce scored 35 league goals from 40 games league appearances during the season. It was not until the 1933–34 season that Wilfred Milne scored his first goal for Swansea at Lincoln City after 501 appearances without a goal. In the 1935–36 season the Swans set a league record for longest distance travelled between consecutive matches, Good Friday Swans played at Plymouth (2–1), and Easter Saturday Swans played at Newcastle United (1–2).</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Post-war_.281945.E2.80.931965.29">Post-war (1945–1965)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Swansea_City_A.F.C.&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Post-war (1945–1965)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Ivor_Allchurch.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1875" data-file-width="1876" height="220" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/85/Ivor_Allchurch.JPG/220px-Ivor_Allchurch.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/85/Ivor_Allchurch.JPG/330px-Ivor_Allchurch.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/85/Ivor_Allchurch.JPG/440px-Ivor_Allchurch.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Ivor_Allchurch.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Ivor_Allchurch" title="Ivor Allchurch">Ivor Allchurch</a> scored 164 goals in 445 appearances for the Swans between 1947–1958 and 1965–1968</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>After just one season back from wartime football, the Swans finished 21st in the <a href="/wiki/Football_League_Second_Division" title="Football League Second Division">Second Division</a>, and thus returned to <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Division_Three_(South)" title="Division Three (South)">Division Three (South)</a> for the first time since 1925. The following season was one of consolidation, however in 1948–1949 the Swans stormed their way to winning the division for the second time. Only one point was dropped at home all season as the feat of the 1925 promotion side was emulated, with the side finishing a whole seven points ahead of second placed Reading. <a href="/wiki/Billy_McCandless" title="Billy McCandless">Billy McCandless</a> was the manager who led the side to promotion, and in doing so he completed a rare <a href="/wiki/Hat-trick" title="Hat-trick">hat-trick</a> of winning the Third Division (South) title with all three <a href="/wiki/South_Wales" title="South Wales">South Wales</a> clubs – and without losing a home game with Swansea or Cardiff.</p>
<p>Following promotion, the Swans had another 15 years of Second Division football to look forward to, however despite what successive managers and chairmen were to say, Swansea Town only once during that time looked like they could genuinely challenge for promotion. That came in the 1955–56 season, when a side containing the likes of <a href="/wiki/Ivor_Allchurch" title="Ivor Allchurch">Ivor Allchurch</a>, <a href="/wiki/Terry_Medwin" title="Terry Medwin">Terry Medwin</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Harry_Griffiths_(footballer_born_1931)" title="Harry Griffiths (footballer born 1931)">Harry Griffiths</a> and Tom Kiley led the table early in the season, before an injury to Kiley, referred to as the <a href="/wiki/Linchpin" title="Linchpin">linchpin</a> of the side, in mid-November led to a decline in form. He was never adequately replaced, but despite this and the sale of some of the club's best players, the side remained in contention for promotion until the beginning of April. Following a 6–1 win over second placed <a href="/wiki/Leicester_City_F.C." title="Leicester City F.C.">Leicester City</a> at the Vetch Field at the end of March the side was just two points behind second placed <a href="/wiki/Liverpool_F.C." title="Liverpool F.C.">Liverpool</a> with a game in hand – however subsequent results were not as encouraging, and they eventually slipped away to finish tenth.</p>
<p>In 1964, the Swans reached a second <a href="/wiki/FA_Cup" title="FA Cup">FA Cup</a> semi-final, beating <a href="/wiki/Barrow_A.F.C." title="Barrow A.F.C.">Barrow</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sheffield_United_F.C." title="Sheffield United F.C.">Sheffield United</a> and <a href="/wiki/Stoke_City_F.C." title="Stoke City F.C.">Stoke City</a> en route to a famous sixth round victory at Anfield. Few gave the Swans, struggling for their lives at the bottom of Division Two, any chance of causing an upset against the league leaders. But the Swans were 0–2 up at half-time thanks to <a href="/wiki/Jim_McLaughlin_(footballer)" title="Jim McLaughlin (footballer)">Jimmy McLaughlin</a> and Eddie Thomas. Liverpool turned up the pressure in the second half, pulling a goal back before being awarded a penalty nine minutes from time. <a href="/wiki/Ronnie_Moran" title="Ronnie Moran">Ronnie Moran</a> had established an excellent record as a <a href="/wiki/Penalty_(rugby)" title="Penalty (rugby)">penalty</a> taker, but he failed to beat the excellent <a href="/wiki/Noel_Dwyer" title="Noel Dwyer">Noel Dwyer</a> on this occasion. Fellow second division side <a href="/wiki/Preston_North_End_F.C." title="Preston North End F.C.">Preston North End</a> awaited in the semi-final at <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Villa_Park_(stadium)" title="Villa Park (stadium)">Villa Park</a>, but despite taking the lead through McLaughlin again, the Swans were to be denied by a second half penalty and a wonder goal from nearly 40 yards.</p>
<p>After flirting with relegation on a few occasions during the previous seasons, the Swans' luck finally ran out a season later in 1965, and they were back in the Third Division.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="A_downward_spiral_.281965.E2.80.931977.29">A downward spiral (1965–1977)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Swansea_City_A.F.C.&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: A downward spiral (1965–1977)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Following relegation, <a href="/wiki/Trevor_Morris_(footballer)" title="Trevor Morris (footballer)">Trevor Morris</a>, who had been manager since 1958, was sacked and <a href="/wiki/Glyn_Davies_(footballer)" title="Glyn Davies (footballer)">Glyn Davies</a>, a former Swansea player, was appointed in his place. Davies re-signed the 36-year-old <a href="/wiki/Ivor_Allchurch" title="Ivor Allchurch">Ivor Allchurch</a> from <a href="/wiki/Cardiff_City_F.C." title="Cardiff City F.C.">Cardiff City</a>, but despite winning the <a href="/wiki/Welsh_Cup" title="Welsh Cup">Welsh Cup</a>, the season saw some of the club's heaviest defeats, and the manager only lasted the season. Relegation to Division Four followed in 1967 and <a href="/wiki/Ivor_Allchurch" title="Ivor Allchurch">Ivor Allchurch</a> retired. The 1967–68 season saw the record attendance of 32,796 at the <a href="/wiki/Vetch_Field" title="Vetch Field">Vetch Field</a> for an <a href="/wiki/FA_Cup" title="FA Cup">FA Cup</a> Fourth Round match against <a href="/wiki/Arsenal_F.C." title="Arsenal F.C.">Arsenal</a>.</p>
<p>A tragedy struck the club on 20 January 1969 when players Roy Evans and Brian Purcell were killed in a car crash on the way to a game.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-10"><a href="#cite_note-10">[10]</a></sup></p>
<p>In 1969, the club name was changed to Swansea City, and <a href="/wiki/Roy_Bentley" title="Roy Bentley">Roy Bentley</a>'s side celebrated by securing promotion back to the Third Division. A record run of 19 matches unbeaten provided the foundations for a promotion challenge in 1971–72, but an awful run towards the end of the season resulted in a mid-table finish. A poor start the following season, combined with falling attendances, saw Bentley resign, and he was replaced by <a href="/wiki/Harry_Gregg" title="Harry Gregg">Harry Gregg</a>. Gregg failed to stop the rot and the club was back in the Fourth Division for 1973–74 season.</p>
<p>A record low crowd of just 1,358 watched the Swans against <a href="/wiki/Northampton_Town_F.C." title="Northampton Town F.C.">Northampton Town</a>, and the following season the Swans were forced to apply for re-election to the football league after a last day defeat at <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Rochdale_F.C." title="Rochdale F.C.">Rochdale</a> condemned them to a 21st-place finish. The application was a success, although by now former player Harry Griffiths had replaced Gregg as manager. Malcolm Struel also took over as <a href="/wiki/Chairman" title="Chairman">chairman</a>, having previously been on the board, and promised a return to former glories, stating that he would not sell the club's best young talent as previous boards had done.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Meteoric_rise_and_equally_rapid_fall_.281977.E2.80.931986.29">Meteoric rise and equally rapid fall (1977–1986)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Swansea_City_A.F.C.&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Meteoric rise and equally rapid fall (1977–1986)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Swansea_City_AFC_League_Performance.svg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="538" data-file-width="1017" height="159" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1e/Swansea_City_AFC_League_Performance.svg/300px-Swansea_City_AFC_League_Performance.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1e/Swansea_City_AFC_League_Performance.svg/450px-Swansea_City_AFC_League_Performance.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1e/Swansea_City_AFC_League_Performance.svg/600px-Swansea_City_AFC_League_Performance.svg.png 2x" width="300"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Swansea_City_AFC_League_Performance.svg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Chart showing the progress of Swansea City A.F.C. through the <a href="/wiki/English_football_league_system" title="English football league system">English football league system</a>.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Despite promising performances during the first half of the 1977–78 season, Harry Griffiths resigned as Swansea City's manager in February 1978, doubting his own ability to take the club any further. The new manager was former <a href="/wiki/Liverpool_F.C." title="Liverpool F.C.">Liverpool</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cardiff_City_F.C." title="Cardiff City F.C.">Cardiff City</a> and <a href="/wiki/Wales_national_football_team" title="Wales national football team">Wales</a> striker <a href="/wiki/John_Toshack" title="John Toshack">John Toshack</a>. On 1 March 1978, at 28 years old, Toshack became the youngest manager in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Football_League" title="Football League">Football League</a>, with Griffiths as his assistant. Thus began a remarkable climb from the <a href="/wiki/Football_League_Fourth_Division" title="Football League Fourth Division">Fourth Division</a> to the top of the entire league. Despite relinquishing his role as manager before the end of the season, this was Griffiths' team, and the promotion from the Fourth Division was largely his doing. During this season, the Swans' record league win was achieved (8–0 against <a href="/wiki/Hartlepool_United_F.C." title="Hartlepool United F.C.">Hartlepool United</a>). Before promotion was secured, however, Harry Griffiths died of a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Heart_attack" title="Heart attack">heart attack</a> on 25 April 1978 before the home game against <a href="/wiki/Scunthorpe_United_F.C." title="Scunthorpe United F.C.">Scunthorpe United</a>.</p>
<p>A further promotion was achieved next season and the club returned to the <a href="/wiki/Football_League_Second_Division" title="Football League Second Division">Second Division</a> after an absence of 14 years, with Toshack himself coming off the bench to score the winning goal against <a href="/wiki/Chesterfield_F.C." title="Chesterfield F.C.">Chesterfield</a> and thus secure promotion.</p>
<p>After a season of consolidation, Swansea City again challenged for promotion and travelled to <a href="/wiki/Preston_North_End_F.C." title="Preston North End F.C.">Preston North End</a> on 2 May 1981 in the knowledge that victory would assure them a place in the <a href="/wiki/Football_League_First_Division" title="Football League First Division">First Division</a> for the first time in the club's history. A 3–1 win guaranteed a third promotion in four seasons and Swansea City joined the footballing elite. The goalscorers on that historic day at Deepdale were <a href="/wiki/Tommy_Craig" title="Tommy Craig">Tommy Craig</a>, <a href="/wiki/Leighton_James" title="Leighton James">Leighton James</a> and <a href="/wiki/Jeremy_Charles" title="Jeremy Charles">Jeremy Charles</a>. The four-year rise from basement to top division is a record in English football, held jointly with <a href="/wiki/Wimbledon_F.C." title="Wimbledon F.C.">Wimbledon F.C.</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-11"><a href="#cite_note-11">[11]</a></sup> Coincidentally, the Swansea decline started the same year as the Wimbledon rise. Swansea also won the Welsh Cup that season, qualifying for Europe for the first time since the 1965–66 season.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-12"><a href="#cite_note-12">[12]</a></sup></p>
<p>The 1981–82 season began as implausibly as recent history had suggested it might. The fixture computer handed Swansea's upstarts a first-day home game against <a href="/wiki/Leeds_United_F.C." title="Leeds United F.C.">Leeds United</a>, which Swansea promptly won 5–1 with a hat-trick by debutant <a href="/wiki/Bob_Latchford" title="Bob Latchford">Bob Latchford</a>. Swansea had swept from the basement division to the top of the entire Football League in barely three years. Victories over footballing royalty such as <a href="/wiki/Liverpool_F.C." title="Liverpool F.C.">Liverpool</a>, <a href="/wiki/Manchester_United_F.C." title="Manchester United F.C.">Manchester United</a>, <a href="/wiki/Arsenal_F.C." title="Arsenal F.C.">Arsenal</a> and <a href="/wiki/Tottenham_Hotspur_F.C." title="Tottenham Hotspur F.C.">Tottenham Hotspur</a> followed as the club topped the league on several further occasions. However, injuries to key players took their toll, and the lack of depth in the squad meant that the season ended in sixth-place finish.</p>
<p>Furthermore, a fateful combination of poor form, misfortune in the transfer market and financial problems led to a slump which was as quick and spectacular as had been the rise: two consecutive relegations followed, and Toshack was sacked. By 1985, the club was battling for its very survival on two fronts. Whilst its creditors lined up a <a href="/wiki/High_Court_of_Justice" title="High Court of Justice">High Court</a> hearing with the aim of liquidating the club, Swansea City had come to rely on a combination of old stagers and young professionals.</p>
<p>Wound up by court order in December 1985, Swansea City was saved by local businessman Doug Sharpe who took over the running of the club, although the change of ownership was not enough to prevent relegation to the <a href="/wiki/Football_League_Fourth_Division" title="Football League Fourth Division">Fourth Division</a> in 1986. Eight years on from the first promotion under Toshack, the club was back where it had started.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="In_place_of_strife_.281986.E2.80.931995.29">In place of strife (1986–1995)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Swansea_City_A.F.C.&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: In place of strife (1986–1995)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Swansea won promotion from the Fourth Division in 1988 – beating <a href="/wiki/Rotherham_United_F.C." title="Rotherham United F.C.">Rotherham United</a> and <a href="/wiki/Torquay_United_F.C." title="Torquay United F.C.">Torquay United</a> over two legs in the inaugural playoffs. They remained in the league's third tier for the next eight seasons – the longest period of stability the club had seen since the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Second_World_War" title="Second World War">war</a>.</p>
<p>Doug Sharpe may have kept the purse strings tight, but under <a href="/wiki/Terry_Yorath" title="Terry Yorath">Terry Yorath</a> and then <a href="/wiki/Frank_Burrows" title="Frank Burrows">Frank Burrows</a>, the club managed to stay in the Second Division, reach the playoff semi-finals in 1993 and make their first <a href="/wiki/Wembley_Stadium" title="Wembley Stadium">Wembley</a> appearance a year later.</p>
<p>Burrows guided the Swans to within 180 minutes of Wembley in 1993 – a run of five wins in the last six league matches (all at home) secured a playoff place, and with five minutes remaining of the first leg of the semi-final against <a href="/wiki/West_Bromwich_Albion_F.C." title="West Bromwich Albion F.C.">West Bromwich Albion</a>, the Swans were 2–0 up. Andy McFarlane scored an <a href="/wiki/Own_goal" title="Own goal">own goal</a> when the ball rebounded off the crossbar then into the net off his knee to give West Brom a lifeline, and two early goals in the second leg gave <i>"the Baggies"</i> the advantage, until midfielder <a href="/wiki/Micky_Mellon" title="Micky Mellon">Micky Mellon</a> was sent off. Burrows threw on <a href="/wiki/Colin_West" title="Colin West">Colin West</a>, however within minutes of coming on the former West Brom striker was sent off, and ended any hopes of a Wembley final.</p>
<p>Although the league campaign the following season did not live up the previous one, mainly due to the sale of key players, Burrows guided the Swans to Wembley for the first time in their history for the final of the Autoglass Trophy. Wins over <a href="/wiki/Plymouth_Argyle_F.C." title="Plymouth Argyle F.C.">Plymouth Argyle</a> &amp; <a href="/wiki/Exeter_City_F.C." title="Exeter City F.C.">Exeter City</a> in the group stage followed by triumphs over Exeter again, <a href="/wiki/Port_Vale_F.C." title="Port Vale F.C.">Port Vale</a>, <a href="/wiki/Leyton_Orient_F.C." title="Leyton Orient F.C.">Leyton Orient</a> and <a href="/wiki/Wycombe_Wanderers_F.C." title="Wycombe Wanderers F.C.">Wycombe Wanderers</a> over two legs saw the Swans play <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Huddersfield_Town_F.C." title="Huddersfield Town F.C.">Huddersfield Town</a> in a final that finished 1–1. Chairman Doug Sharpe brought back the famous hat, and the Swans went on to win 3–1 on penalties.</p>
<p>The following season failed to live up to expectations, although the club again reached the semi-finals of the Auto Windscreens Shield, eventually going out to <a href="/wiki/Birmingham_City_F.C." title="Birmingham City F.C.">Birmingham City</a>, and an eventful FA Cup run saw them win at <a href="/wiki/Middlesbrough_F.C." title="Middlesbrough F.C.">Middlesbrough</a> in a third round replay, before going out to Newcastle United at <a href="/wiki/St_James%27_Park" title="St James' Park">St James' Park</a>.</p>
<p>The 1995–96 season ended with relegation back to the third division after eight years. The Swans were doing fine around Christmas time, but a complete collapse in the second half of the season, including a 7–0 FA Cup defeat at third division <a href="/wiki/Fulham_F.C." title="Fulham F.C.">Fulham</a>, 4–0 and 5–1 defeats at Blackpool and <a href="/wiki/Oxford_United_F.C." title="Oxford United F.C.">Oxford United</a> respectively, relegation was inevitable, despite the arrival of <a href="/wiki/Jan_M%C3%B8lby" title="Jan Mølby">Jan Mølby</a>.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="The_difficult_years_return_.281995.E2.80.932001.29">The difficult years return (1995–2001)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Swansea_City_A.F.C.&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: The difficult years return (1995–2001)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Relegation" title="Relegation">Relegation</a> in 1996 was accompanied by an unfortunate statistic: never before had the club been managed by four men in the same season. Most embarrassing was the appointment of <a href="/wiki/Kevin_Cullis" title="Kevin Cullis">Kevin Cullis</a> as manager by a <a href="/wiki/Consortium" title="Consortium">consortium</a> wishing to buy the club. Cullis, whose previous experience was with <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Non-league" title="Non-league">non-league</a> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/English_Midlands" title="English Midlands">Midlands</a> club <a href="/wiki/Cradley_Town_F.C." title="Cradley Town F.C.">Cradley Town</a> youth team, was certainly not the "big name" manager promised by the new owners. Alarmed at developments at the club, outgoing chairman Doug Sharpe invoked a contractual clause to cancel the deal and resumed control himself: Cullis was promptly sacked after just six days. During his short-lived reign, his evident lack of ability led to senior players <a href="/wiki/Christian_Edwards" title="Christian Edwards">Christian Edwards</a> and <a href="/wiki/Dave_Penney" title="Dave Penney">Dave Penney</a> ejecting Cullis from the dressing room during half time and giving the team talk themselves in a 4–0 defeat to <a href="/wiki/Blackpool_F.C." title="Blackpool F.C.">Blackpool</a>, which proved to be his second and last game in charge.</p>
<p>Cullis's successor was the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Danish_people" title="Danish people">Dane</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jan_M%C3%B8lby" title="Jan Mølby">Jan Mølby</a>, a former <a href="/wiki/Liverpool_F.C." title="Liverpool F.C.">Liverpool</a> player taking his first steps in management. His appointment inevitably prompted comparison with the Toshack era which began nearly 20 years earlier. Despite relegation in 1996, the club reached the final of the 1997 <a href="/wiki/Football_League_Third_Division" title="Football League Third Division">Third Division</a> promotion play-offs but lost to <a href="/wiki/Northampton_Town_F.C." title="Northampton Town F.C.">Northampton Town</a>, whose goal came from a re-taken free kick by <a href="/wiki/John_Frain" title="John Frain">John Frain</a> in the final minute. Mølby was sacked just weeks into the following season, with Swansea struggling near the foot of the league. After the initial optimism, the Liverpool connection had not caused history to repeat itself.</p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Alan_Cork" title="Alan Cork">Alan Cork</a> was appointed as manager, but was dismissed after leading the club to its lowest league finish for 23 years. <a href="/wiki/John_Hollins" title="John Hollins">John Hollins</a> was appointed, and things soon started to improve. In 1999, the club reached the promotion <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Play-offs" title="Play-offs">playoffs</a>, only to lose in extra time at <a href="/wiki/Scunthorpe_United_F.C." title="Scunthorpe United F.C.">Scunthorpe United</a>. The season was also notable for a third round <a href="/wiki/FA_Cup" title="FA Cup">FA Cup</a> victory over <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/FA_Premier_League" title="FA Premier League">Premiership</a> opponents <a href="/wiki/West_Ham_United_F.C." title="West Ham United F.C.">West Ham United</a>, whose team included <a href="/wiki/Frank_Lampard" title="Frank Lampard">Frank Lampard</a>, <a href="/wiki/Joe_Cole" title="Joe Cole">Joe Cole</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rio_Ferdinand" title="Rio Ferdinand">Rio Ferdinand</a> and <a href="/wiki/John_Hartson" title="John Hartson">John Hartson</a>. Swansea thus became the first <a href="/wiki/Football_League_Third_Division" title="Football League Third Division">bottom division</a> team to defeat a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/FA_Premier_League" title="FA Premier League">Premiership</a> club in the <a href="/wiki/FA_Cup" title="FA Cup">FA Cup</a> since the re-organisation of the league structure in 1992.</p>
<p>The club was promoted in 2000 as <a href="/wiki/Football_League_Third_Division" title="Football League Third Division">Division Three</a> champions, following a nail-biting championship decider on the final day of the season against second-placed <a href="/wiki/Rotherham_United_F.C." title="Rotherham United F.C.">Rotherham United</a>. Hollins' side certainly proved to be effective and functional, rather than pretty, seemingly winning 1–0 every week on their way to the title. The side conceded just 32 goals during the <a href="/wiki/1999%E2%80%932000_Swansea_City_A.F.C._season" title="1999–2000 Swansea City A.F.C. season">1999–2000 season</a>, largely due to the form of excellent centre-back pairing Jason Smith and <a href="/wiki/Matthew_Bound" title="Matthew Bound">Matthew Bound</a>, as well as <a href="/wiki/Goalkeeper_(association_football)" title="Goalkeeper (association football)">'keeper</a> <a href="/wiki/Roger_Freestone" title="Roger Freestone">Roger Freestone</a>. During the season the side set a record of nine consecutive league victories, and, during the same period, seven consecutive clean sheets. Striker <a href="/wiki/Walter_Boyd_(footballer)" title="Walter Boyd (footballer)">Walter Boyd</a> also set an unwanted record of being the fastest substitute ever sent off, when he was red-carded for striking a <a href="/wiki/Darlington_F.C." title="Darlington F.C.">Darlington</a> player seconds after being brought on and before play had resumed, therefore being officially recorded as zero seconds.</p>
<p>Promotion was secured courtesy of a 3–0 win over <a href="/wiki/Exeter_City_F.C." title="Exeter City F.C.">Exeter City</a> at a packed <a href="/wiki/Vetch_Field" title="Vetch Field">Vetch Field</a>. However, the following week's 1–1 draw at <a href="/wiki/Rotherham_United_F.C." title="Rotherham United F.C.">Rotherham United</a>, which confirmed Swansea as Division Three Champions, was overshadowed by the death of supporter Terry Coles, who was trampled to death by a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Police_horse" title="Police horse">police horse</a> in narrow Millmoor Lane before the game.</p>
<p>Despite significant optimism on the terraces, it was clear that the team was not strong enough to survive in the higher division and relegation occurred in May 2001, just 12 months after promotion. Hollins had failed to strengthen the side at all during the summer, and despite a decent start, a 5–1 defeat at big-spending <a href="/wiki/Reading_F.C." title="Reading F.C.">Reading</a> in September led to a disastrous slide down the table, and the side won just eight games all season, and were saved from bottom spot only by <a href="/wiki/Oxford_United_F.C." title="Oxford United F.C.">Oxford United</a> being even worse. Hollins' certainly was not helped by lack of investment from the board and injury to key players, but the fans patience wore thin as his continual insistence that the squad was good enough to survive grew more comical by the week. Relegation seemed certain following a 5–3 defeat at fellow strugglers <a href="/wiki/Luton_Town_F.C." title="Luton Town F.C.">Luton Town</a>, where <a href="/wiki/Giovanni_Savarese" title="Giovanni Savarese">Giovanni Savarese</a> scored a hat-trick, however Hollins' maintained that the side could stay up, even when 18 points were needed from the final six matches, and for two other teams to pick up no more points.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Last_years_at_Vetch_Field_and_return_to_League_One_.282001.E2.80.932005.29">Last years at Vetch Field and return to League One (2001–2005)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Swansea_City_A.F.C.&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Last years at Vetch Field and return to League One (2001–2005)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Vetch_45.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1704" data-file-width="2272" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/98/Vetch_45.JPG/220px-Vetch_45.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/98/Vetch_45.JPG/330px-Vetch_45.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/98/Vetch_45.JPG/440px-Vetch_45.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Vetch_45.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Swansea fans and players celebrate the last league goal to be scored at the <a href="/wiki/Vetch_Field" title="Vetch Field">Vetch Field</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In July 2001, following relegation back to <a href="/wiki/Football_League_Third_Division" title="Football League Third Division">Third Division</a>, the club was sold to managing director Mike Lewis for £1. Lewis subsequently sold on his stake to a consortium of <a href="/wiki/Australia" title="Australia">Australian</a> businessmen behind the <a href="/wiki/Brisbane_Lions" title="Brisbane Lions">Brisbane Lions</a> (An Australian Rules Football team that is based in Brisbane) football team, fronted by Tony Petty. Seven players were sacked and eight others saw their contracts terminated, angering supporters and sanctions were threatened by <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/The_Football_League" title="The Football League">the Football League</a> with a rival consortium headed by ex-player <a href="/wiki/Mel_Nurse" title="Mel Nurse">Mel Nurse</a> seeking to buy out the new owners. During this period Hollins was sacked after a poor start to the season, and <a href="/wiki/Colin_Addison" title="Colin Addison">Colin Addison</a> took over as manager. The turmoil led to the creation of the Swansea City <a href="/wiki/Supporters%27_trust" title="Supporters' trust">Supporters' Trust</a>, which sought to save the club and ultimately guarantee supporter representation on the club's board.</p>
<p>The Petty group sold its stake in January 2002 after a bitter stand-off with the Nurse consortium, which was supported by the majority of the club's fans. Jim Moore and Mel Griffin, previously rescuers of Hull City FC, stepped into the breach and persuaded Petty to sell to them (as he had promised to bankrupt the club &amp; make it extinct rather than sell to Nurse). From there Moore became Chairman for three weeks giving the "Mel Nurse Consortium" time to organize its finances. Having successfully reorganized the finances of Hull City FC, both Moore &amp; Griffin were believers in clubs belonging in the hands of local people, and so believing Nurses group were best for The Swans, subsequently passed the club onto Nurses consortium for the fee of £1. Despite problems off the pitch, Addison's side had managed a mid-table position, but lack of funds led to his dismissal in early March, and under <a href="/wiki/Nick_Cusack" title="Nick Cusack">Nick Cusack</a> the club slumped to a 20th placed-finish. Cusack lasted just eight games into the following season, and was sacked after a 1–0 defeat at league debutants <a href="/wiki/Boston_United_F.C." title="Boston United F.C.">Boston United</a> had put the Swans on the bottom of the Football League for the first time in its 91-year history. He was replaced by <a href="/wiki/Brian_Flynn" title="Brian Flynn">Brian Flynn</a>. Swansea City avoided relegation to the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Football_Conference" title="Football Conference">Football Conference</a> on the last day of the season, at the expense of <a href="/wiki/Exeter_City_F.C." title="Exeter City F.C.">Exeter City</a>, a club then vice-chaired by Mike Lewis.</p>
<p>Brian Flynn's side finished 2003–04 10th and reached the fifth round of the FA Cup for the first time in 24 years, eventually losing 2–1 at <a href="/wiki/Tranmere_Rovers_F.C." title="Tranmere Rovers F.C.">Tranmere Rovers</a>. Flynn was dismissed and replaced by <a href="/wiki/Kenny_Jackett" title="Kenny Jackett">Kenny Jackett</a>. Jackett lost his first six matches in charge, ending any hope of a play-off place. The following season Jackett recruited a number of new defensive players and set a record of seven consecutive home clean sheets, all victories. The Swans' last season at the Vetch Field saw the club win promotion on the last day of the season, clinching a 3rd-placed finish with a 1–0 win away to <a href="/wiki/Bury_F.C." title="Bury F.C.">Bury</a>. Their last league game at their old ground was a 1–0 win over <a href="/wiki/Shrewsbury_Town_F.C." title="Shrewsbury Town F.C.">Shrewsbury Town</a>, with the last game of any sort being a 2–1 win against <a href="/wiki/Wrexham_A.F.C." title="Wrexham A.F.C.">Wrexham</a> in the final of the 2005 <a href="/wiki/FAW_Premier_Cup" title="FAW Premier Cup">FAW Premier Cup</a>.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Move_to_the_Liberty_Stadium_and_return_to_the_top_flight_.282005.E2.80.932011.29">Move to the Liberty Stadium and return to the top flight (2005–2011)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Swansea_City_A.F.C.&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Move to the Liberty Stadium and return to the top flight (2005–2011)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:204px">
<div style="position: relative;font-size:80%">

<div style="text-align:center; font-size:smaller"><a href="/wiki/2011_Football_League_Championship_play-off_Final" title="2011 Football League Championship play-off Final">2011 Football League Championship play-off Final</a> starting line-up</div>

</div>
<p>The club moved to the new <a href="/wiki/Liberty_Stadium" title="Liberty Stadium">Liberty Stadium</a> during the summer of 2005. The first competitive game was a 1–0 victory against <a href="/wiki/Tranmere_Rovers_F.C." title="Tranmere Rovers F.C.">Tranmere Rovers</a> in August 2005. In their first season back in League One, Swansea, after beating <a href="/wiki/Brentford_F.C." title="Brentford F.C.">Brentford</a> in the semi-finals, lost on <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Penalty_shootout_(association_football)" title="Penalty shootout (association football)">penalties</a> to <a href="/wiki/Barnsley_F.C." title="Barnsley F.C.">Barnsley</a> in the final at the <a href="/wiki/Millennium_Stadium" title="Millennium Stadium">Millennium Stadium</a> in Cardiff. That same season, Swansea won the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Football_League_Trophy" title="Football League Trophy">Football League Trophy</a> for the first time since 1994, and the <a href="/wiki/FAW_Premier_Cup" title="FAW Premier Cup">FAW Premier Cup</a> for a second successive year.</p>
<p>In the following season Jackett resigned as manager in mid-season to be replaced by <a href="/wiki/Roberto_Mart%C3%ADnez" title="Roberto Martínez">Roberto Martínez</a>. Martínez's arrival saw an improvement in form, but Swansea missed out on the play-offs again. The following season, an 18-game unbeaten run helped them to the League One title. The club amassed a total of 92 points over the course of the season, the highest ever by a Welsh club in the Football League. Five Swansea players were in the PFA Team of the Year, including the division's 29-goal top scorer <a href="/wiki/Jason_Scotland" title="Jason Scotland">Jason Scotland</a>. That same season Swansea lost on penalties to <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Milton_Keynes_Dons" title="Milton Keynes Dons">Milton Keynes Dons</a> in the area final of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Football_League_Trophy" title="Football League Trophy">Football League Trophy</a>.</p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Swansea_City_AFC_Championship_Play_Off_Winners_2011.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="480" data-file-width="720" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/14/Swansea_City_AFC_Championship_Play_Off_Winners_2011.jpg/220px-Swansea_City_AFC_Championship_Play_Off_Winners_2011.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/14/Swansea_City_AFC_Championship_Play_Off_Winners_2011.jpg/330px-Swansea_City_AFC_Championship_Play_Off_Winners_2011.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/14/Swansea_City_AFC_Championship_Play_Off_Winners_2011.jpg/440px-Swansea_City_AFC_Championship_Play_Off_Winners_2011.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Swansea_City_AFC_Championship_Play_Off_Winners_2011.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Swansea City celebrate promotion to the Premier League at <a href="/wiki/Wembley_Stadium" title="Wembley Stadium">Wembley Stadium</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Upon returning to the second tier of English football after 24 years Swansea City finished the 2008–09 season in eighth place, and missed out on the play-offs the following season by a single point. After an impressive 63 wins in 126 games for Swansea City, Martínez left for <a href="/wiki/Wigan_Athletic_F.C." title="Wigan Athletic F.C.">Wigan Athletic</a> on the 15 June 2009 with his tenure returning just 26 losses in that time. He was replaced by Portuguese <a href="/wiki/Paulo_Sousa" title="Paulo Sousa">Paulo Sousa</a> who adopted a more defensive style of play whilst also retaining the slick and effective continental game of "<a href="/wiki/Tiki-taka" title="Tiki-taka">tiki-taka</a>" football that was installed by his immediate predecessor. Sousa subsequently left Swansea to take charge at <a href="/wiki/Leicester_City_F.C." title="Leicester City F.C.">Leicester City</a> on 5 July 2010, lasting just one year and 13 days in South Wales. However, just before the departure of Sousa, on 15 May 2010, Swansea player <a href="/wiki/Besian_Idrizaj" title="Besian Idrizaj">Besian Idrizaj</a> tragically suffered a heart attack in his native Austria while on international duty. The club retired the number 40 shirt in his memory, and the players wore shirts dedicated to Idrizaj after their victory in the play-off final.</p>
<p>Northern Irishman <a href="/wiki/Brendan_Rodgers" title="Brendan Rodgers">Brendan Rodgers</a> took charge for the 2010–11 season. He guided the club to a third-placed finish and qualification for the Championship play-offs, with the new manager again keeping the continental style of play introduced by Martínez. After beating <a href="/wiki/Nottingham_Forest_F.C." title="Nottingham Forest F.C.">Nottingham Forest</a> 3–1 on aggregate in the semi-final they defeated <a href="/wiki/Reading_F.C." title="Reading F.C.">Reading</a> 4–2 in <a href="/wiki/2011_Football_League_Championship_play-off_Final" title="2011 Football League Championship play-off Final">the final</a> at <a href="/wiki/Wembley_Stadium" title="Wembley Stadium">Wembley Stadium</a>, with <a href="/wiki/Scott_Sinclair" title="Scott Sinclair">Scott Sinclair</a> scoring a hat-trick.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-13"><a href="#cite_note-13">[13]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Premier_League_.26_Europe_.282011.E2.80.93present.29">Premier League &amp; Europe (2011–present)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Swansea_City_A.F.C.&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Premier League &amp; Europe (2011–present)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>

<div style="position:relative; text-align:center; left:-11px; top:-8px; width:22px; height:15px; line-height:0"><span class="flagicon"><a href="/wiki/England" title="England"><img alt="England" class="thumbborder" data-file-height="480" data-file-width="800" height="13" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/b/be/Flag_of_England.svg/22px-Flag_of_England.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/b/be/Flag_of_England.svg/33px-Flag_of_England.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/b/be/Flag_of_England.svg/44px-Flag_of_England.svg.png 2x" width="22"/></a></span></div>
<div style="position:relative; text-align:center; left: -5em; top:-0.65em; width:10em; line-height:1.4em; white-space:nowrap"><a href="/wiki/Wayne_Routledge" title="Wayne Routledge">Routledge</a></div>
</div>
<div style="position:absolute; z-index:2; top:70%; left:50%; height: 0; width: 0; margin: 0; padding: 0;">
<div style="position:relative; text-align:center; left:-11px; top:-8px; width:22px; height:15px; line-height:0"><span class="flagicon"><a href="/wiki/Spain" title="Spain"><img alt="Spain" class="thumbborder" data-file-height="500" data-file-width="750" height="15" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/9a/Flag_of_Spain.svg/22px-Flag_of_Spain.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/9a/Flag_of_Spain.svg/33px-Flag_of_Spain.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/9a/Flag_of_Spain.svg/44px-Flag_of_Spain.svg.png 2x" width="22"/></a></span></div>
<div style="position:relative; text-align:center; left: -5em; top:-0.65em; width:10em; line-height:1.4em; white-space:nowrap"><a href="/wiki/Pablo_Hern%C3%A1ndez_(footballer,_born_1985)" title="Pablo Hernández (footballer, born 1985)">Hernández</a></div>
</div>
<div style="position:absolute; z-index:2; top:82%; left:50%; height: 0; width: 0; margin: 0; padding: 0;">
<div style="position:relative; text-align:center; left:-11px; top:-8px; width:22px; height:15px; line-height:0"><span class="flagicon"><a href="/wiki/Spain" title="Spain"><img alt="Spain" class="thumbborder" data-file-height="500" data-file-width="750" height="15" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/9a/Flag_of_Spain.svg/22px-Flag_of_Spain.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/9a/Flag_of_Spain.svg/33px-Flag_of_Spain.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/9a/Flag_of_Spain.svg/44px-Flag_of_Spain.svg.png 2x" width="22"/></a></span></div>
<div style="position:relative; text-align:center; left: -5em; top:-0.65em; width:10em; line-height:1.4em; white-space:nowrap"><a href="/wiki/Michu" title="Michu">Michu</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<div style="text-align:center; font-size:smaller"><a href="/wiki/2013_Football_League_Cup_Final" title="2013 Football League Cup Final">2013 Football League Cup Final</a> starting line-up</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>By being promoted to the Premier League for the <a href="/wiki/2011%E2%80%9312_Premier_League" title="2011–12 Premier League">2011–12</a> season, Swansea became the first Welsh team to play in the division since its formation in 1992. Swansea signed <a href="/wiki/Danny_Graham_(footballer)" title="Danny Graham (footballer)">Danny Graham</a> from <a href="/wiki/Watford_F.C." title="Watford F.C.">Watford</a> for a then-record fee of £3.5 million. They defeated <a href="/wiki/Arsenal_F.C." title="Arsenal F.C.">Arsenal</a>, <a href="/wiki/Liverpool_F.C." title="Liverpool F.C.">Liverpool</a> and <a href="/wiki/Manchester_City_F.C." title="Manchester City F.C.">Manchester City</a>, the eventual champions, at home during the season. Swansea finished their debut Premier League season in 11th, but at the end of the season <a href="/wiki/Brendan_Rodgers" title="Brendan Rodgers">Brendan Rodgers</a> left to manage Liverpool. He was replaced by <a href="/wiki/Michael_Laudrup" title="Michael Laudrup">Michael Laudrup</a> for the <a href="/wiki/2012%E2%80%9313_Premier_League" title="2012–13 Premier League">2012–13 Premier League season</a>. His first league game ended in a 0–5 victory over <a href="/wiki/Queens_Park_Rangers_F.C." title="Queens Park Rangers F.C.">Queens Park Rangers</a> away at <a href="/wiki/Loftus_Road" title="Loftus Road">Loftus Road</a>. This saw Swansea joint top of the Premier League, making it the first time since October 1981 the team had been at the summit of the top tier. Swansea then went top for two hours after beating <a href="/wiki/West_Ham_United_F.C." title="West Ham United F.C.">West Ham United</a> 3–0 at the <a href="/wiki/Liberty_Stadium" title="Liberty Stadium">Liberty Stadium</a>, with <a href="/wiki/Michu" title="Michu">Michu</a> scoring his third goal in two games.</p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Swansea_City_AFC_logo_(100th_anniversary).svg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="68" data-file-width="74" height="184" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/7/72/Swansea_City_AFC_logo_%28100th_anniversary%29.svg/200px-Swansea_City_AFC_logo_%28100th_anniversary%29.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/7/72/Swansea_City_AFC_logo_%28100th_anniversary%29.svg/300px-Swansea_City_AFC_logo_%28100th_anniversary%29.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/7/72/Swansea_City_AFC_logo_%28100th_anniversary%29.svg/400px-Swansea_City_AFC_logo_%28100th_anniversary%29.svg.png 2x" width="200"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Swansea_City_AFC_logo_(100th_anniversary).svg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The Swansea City A.F.C. centenary crest used during the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/2012-13_Swansea_City_A.F.C._season" title="2012-13 Swansea City A.F.C. season">2012–13 season</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>On 15 October 2012, the board of directors announced that the club had made a profit of £14.2 million after their first season in the Premier League,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-14"><a href="#cite_note-14">[14]</a></sup> and that the expansion of the Liberty Stadium will be conducted in two separate phases when the timing is right for the club.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-15"><a href="#cite_note-15">[15]</a></sup> On 1 December, Swansea picked up a 0–2 away win against Arsenal, with Michu scoring twice during the last minutes of the game, in Swansea's first win at Arsenal in three decades.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-16"><a href="#cite_note-16">[16]</a></sup></p>
<p>On 24 February 2013, Swansea beat <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bradford_City_A.F.C" title="Bradford City A.F.C">Bradford City</a> 0–5 in the <a href="/wiki/2013_Football_League_Cup_Final" title="2013 Football League Cup Final">League Cup final</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-17"><a href="#cite_note-17">[17]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-18"><a href="#cite_note-18">[18]</a></sup> This triumph, in a record victory, was Swansea's first major piece of silverware. On 8 April 2013, Swansea announced record profits of £15.9 million for six months up to November 2012, including an 11% increase in commercial revenue. Swansea finished the season in ninth place in the Premier League, improving upon the league standing achieved in the previous season. On 11 July, Swansea paid a club record transfer fee of £12 million to secure the signing of striker <a href="/wiki/Wilfried_Bony" title="Wilfried Bony">Wilfried Bony</a> from <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Vitesse_Arnhem" title="Vitesse Arnhem">Vitesse Arnhem</a>; Bony was the leading goalscorer in the <a href="/wiki/2012%E2%80%9313_Eredivisie" title="2012–13 Eredivisie">2012–13 Eredivisie</a> with 31 goals and was named Dutch Player of the Year.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-19"><a href="#cite_note-19">[19]</a></sup></p>
<p>On 3 November 2013, Swansea City became the first team to lose a Welsh Premier League derby ever after losing 1–0 to Cardiff City.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-20"><a href="#cite_note-20">[20]</a></sup> However, Swansea City went on to beat Cardiff City 3–0 at the Liberty Stadium on 8 February 2014.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-21"><a href="#cite_note-21">[21]</a></sup></p>
<p>In February 2014, Laudrup was dismissed from the club. Defender <a href="/wiki/Garry_Monk" title="Garry Monk">Garry Monk</a>, a Swansea player since 2004, was named as his replacement.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-22"><a href="#cite_note-22">[22]</a></sup></p>
<p>During the January 2015 transfer window, Wilfried Bony was sold to Manchester City for a record sale of £25 million, with add-ons that could lead to £28 million. This deal eclipsed the record fee received from Liverpool for <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Joe_Allen_(footballer,_born_1990)" title="Joe Allen (footballer, born 1990)">Joe Allen</a>, £15 million.</p>
<p>Swansea City finished eighth in the Premier League at the end of the 2014–15 season with 56 points, their highest position and points haul for a Premier League season, and second highest finish in the top flight of all time. During the season, they produced league doubles over Arsenal and Manchester United, becoming only the third team in Premier League history to achieve that feat.</p>
<p>On 9 December 2015, Swansea City announced that they had parted ways with manager Garry Monk after one win in eleven matches.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-23"><a href="#cite_note-23">[23]</a></sup> The club, after a period with Alan Curtis acting as caretaker manager for the third time, chose the Italian former <a href="/wiki/Udinese_Calcio" title="Udinese Calcio">Udinese Calcio</a> coach <a href="/wiki/Francesco_Guidolin" title="Francesco Guidolin">Francesco Guidolin</a>. During the 2016–17 preseason, Swansea City came under new ownership by an American consortium led by <a href="/wiki/Jason_Levien" title="Jason Levien">Jason Levien</a> and Steve Kaplan, who bought a controlling interest in the club in July 2016.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-24"><a href="#cite_note-24">[24]</a></sup> The takeover was confirmed by Swansea City, but chairman <a href="/wiki/Huw_Jenkins_(Welsh_businessman)" title="Huw Jenkins (Welsh businessman)">Huw Jenkins</a> remained at the club.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-25"><a href="#cite_note-25">[25]</a></sup> On 3 October 2016, Guidolin was sacked and replaced by American coach <a href="/wiki/Bob_Bradley" title="Bob Bradley">Bob Bradley</a> as the club's new manager. The selection of Bradley marked the first time a Premier League club had ever hired an American manager.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-26"><a href="#cite_note-26">[26]</a></sup> Bradley himself was sacked after just 85 days in charge; he won only two of his 11 games, conceded 29 goals, and left with a win percentage of just 18.1%.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-27"><a href="#cite_note-27">[27]</a></sup></p>
<p>On 3 January 2017, <a href="/wiki/FC_Bayern_Munich" title="FC Bayern Munich">Bayern Munich</a> assistant manager <a href="/wiki/Paul_Clement_(football_manager)" title="Paul Clement (football manager)">Paul Clement</a> agreed to take charge of the team, replacing Bradley.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Clement_28-0"><a href="#cite_note-Clement-28">[28]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Stadium">Stadium</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Swansea_City_A.F.C.&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Stadium">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Vetch_Field" title="Vetch Field">Vetch Field</a> and <a href="/wiki/Liberty_Stadium" title="Liberty Stadium">Liberty Stadium</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Vetch_Field.DSC00100.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1224" data-file-width="1632" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ef/Vetch_Field.DSC00100.JPG/220px-Vetch_Field.DSC00100.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ef/Vetch_Field.DSC00100.JPG/330px-Vetch_Field.DSC00100.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ef/Vetch_Field.DSC00100.JPG/440px-Vetch_Field.DSC00100.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Vetch_Field.DSC00100.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The <a href="/wiki/Vetch_Field" title="Vetch Field">Vetch Field</a> was the home of Swansea City for 93 years.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Before Swansea Town was established, children would play football on waste ground in which a plant, called "<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Vetch" title="Vetch">vetch</a>" (a type of legume) was grown. The site was owned by Swansea Gaslight Company in 1912, but was deemed surplus to requirements at the Gas Company. So Swansea Town moved in when they were established in 1912.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ClubHistory_29-0"><a href="#cite_note-ClubHistory-29">[29]</a></sup> The ground originally held 12,000, but hit its peak attendance of 32,786 in an <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/FA_Cup_1967-68" title="FA Cup 1967-68">1967 FA cup</a> Fifth Round against <a href="/wiki/Arsenal_F.C." title="Arsenal F.C.">Arsenal</a>. The last league goal ever scored at the Vetch was scored by <a href="/wiki/Adrian_Forbes" title="Adrian Forbes">Adrian Forbes</a>, on 30 April 2005, as Swansea beat <a href="/wiki/Shrewsbury_Town_F.C." title="Shrewsbury Town F.C.">Shrewsbury Town</a> 1–0.</p>
<p>With a rapidly deteriorating Vetch Field, Swansea looked to relocate. As Swansea and the <a href="/wiki/Ospreys_(rugby_team)" title="Ospreys (rugby team)">Ospreys</a> did not have the capital to invest in a new stadium, the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/City_and_County_of_Swansea_council" title="City and County of Swansea council">Swansea City Council</a> and a developer-led consortia submitted a proposal for a sustainable "bowl" venue for 20,520 seats on a site to the west of the river on the site of the <a href="/wiki/Morfa_Stadium" title="Morfa Stadium">Morfa Stadium</a>, which the Council owned. It was funded by a 355,000 ft retail park on land to the east of the river. The final value of the development being in excess of £50 million. On 23 July 2005, The <a href="/wiki/Liberty_Stadium" title="Liberty Stadium">Liberty Stadium</a> was officially opened as Swansea faced <a href="/wiki/Fulham_F.C." title="Fulham F.C.">Fulham</a> in a <a href="/wiki/Exhibition_game" title="Exhibition game">friendly game</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-LibertyStadium_30-0"><a href="#cite_note-LibertyStadium-30">[30]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:New_Morfa_Stadium_-_geograph.org.uk_-_32243.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="437" data-file-width="640" height="150" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/68/New_Morfa_Stadium_-_geograph.org.uk_-_32243.jpg/220px-New_Morfa_Stadium_-_geograph.org.uk_-_32243.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/68/New_Morfa_Stadium_-_geograph.org.uk_-_32243.jpg/330px-New_Morfa_Stadium_-_geograph.org.uk_-_32243.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/68/New_Morfa_Stadium_-_geograph.org.uk_-_32243.jpg/440px-New_Morfa_Stadium_-_geograph.org.uk_-_32243.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:New_Morfa_Stadium_-_geograph.org.uk_-_32243.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The <a href="/wiki/Liberty_Stadium" title="Liberty Stadium">Liberty Stadium</a> became Swansea City's home ground from 2005.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The Liberty Stadium capacity was 20,532 though has been increased to 20,750<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (September 2012)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup>. The highest attendance recorded at the stadium came against <a href="/wiki/Arsenal_F.C." title="Arsenal F.C.">Arsenal</a> on 31 October 2015 with 20,937 spectators,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-31"><a href="#cite_note-31">[31]</a></sup> beating the previous record of 20,845. The stadium has also hosted three <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Welsh_national_football_team" title="Welsh national football team">Welsh international football</a> matches; the first being a 0–0 draw with <a href="/wiki/Bulgaria_national_football_team" title="Bulgaria national football team">Bulgaria</a> in 2006,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-32"><a href="#cite_note-32">[32]</a></sup> the second a 2–1 defeat to <a href="/wiki/Georgia_national_football_team" title="Georgia national football team">Georgia</a> in 2008 and a 2–0 win over <a href="/wiki/Switzerland_national_football_team" title="Switzerland national football team">Switzerland</a> on 7 October 2011. The first international goal to be scored at the Liberty Stadium was a 25-yard effort from Welsh international <a href="/wiki/Jason_Koumas" title="Jason Koumas">Jason Koumas</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-33"><a href="#cite_note-33">[33]</a></sup></p>
<p>On 1 July 2012, it was widely reported in national media that Swansea City were beginning the planning phase for expanding the Liberty Stadium by approximately 12,000 seats. This plan would be conditional on a successful second season in the Premier League and could cost up to £15 million; the increase would result in a capacity of approximately 32,000 seats.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-34"><a href="#cite_note-34">[34]</a></sup> Later that same year, the board of directors announced that planning applications were to be put forward to the council authority, making the Liberty Stadium the largest sportsclub-owned stadium in Wales.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-35"><a href="#cite_note-35">[35]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Rivalries">Rivalries</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Swansea_City_A.F.C.&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Rivalries">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/South_Wales_derby" title="South Wales derby">South Wales derby</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Dean,_Mike_(2).jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="463" data-file-width="358" height="285" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e3/Dean%2C_Mike_%282%29.jpg/220px-Dean%2C_Mike_%282%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e3/Dean%2C_Mike_%282%29.jpg/330px-Dean%2C_Mike_%282%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/e/e3/Dean%2C_Mike_%282%29.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Dean,_Mike_(2).jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Referee <a href="/wiki/Mike_Dean_(referee)" title="Mike Dean (referee)">Mike Dean</a> receiving treatment after being struck by a projectile in a <a href="/wiki/South_Wales_derby" title="South Wales derby">South Wales derby</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Swansea City's main rivals are <a href="/wiki/Cardiff_City_F.C." title="Cardiff City F.C.">Cardiff City</a>, with the rivalry described as among the most hostile in British football.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-36"><a href="#cite_note-36">[36]</a></sup> Matches between these two clubs are known as the <a href="/wiki/South_Wales_derby" title="South Wales derby">South Wales derbies</a> and are usually one of the highlights of the season for both sets of supporters. To a lesser extent, Swansea City's other rivals are <a href="/wiki/Bristol_City_F.C." title="Bristol City F.C.">Bristol City</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bristol_Rovers_F.C." title="Bristol Rovers F.C.">Bristol Rovers</a> and <a href="/wiki/Newport_County_A.F.C." title="Newport County A.F.C.">Newport County</a>. However, Swansea very rarely meet Newport as they are currently separated by three divisions, while the two clubs share a mutual rivalry with Cardiff City.</p>
<p>Swansea have won 36 of the 106 competitive meetings, compared to Cardiff's 43, who also have the biggest result between the two sides with Swansea losing 5–0 in 1965, with a further 27 drawn; to this day, neither team has done the double. Following Swansea City's promotion to the Championship, the clubs were drawn in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Football_League_Cup" title="Football League Cup">League Cup</a> which would be the first meeting between both sides for nine years.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-37"><a href="#cite_note-37">[37]</a></sup> Swansea City won the tie with a solitary goal from a deflected free-kick taken by <a href="/wiki/Jordi_G%C3%B3mez" title="Jordi Gómez">Jordi Gómez</a>. The match saw sets of supporters from both clubs clash with police after the match.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-38"><a href="#cite_note-38">[38]</a></sup> The next two league games both finished in 2–2 draws.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-39"><a href="#cite_note-39">[39]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-40"><a href="#cite_note-40">[40]</a></sup> However, the derby game at <a href="/wiki/Ninian_Park" title="Ninian Park">Ninian Park</a> was marred with controversy as referee <a href="/wiki/Mike_Dean_(referee)" title="Mike Dean (referee)">Mike Dean</a> was struck by a coin from a Cardiff City supporter.</p>
<p>In the 2009–10 season, Swansea beat Cardiff 3–2 at the Liberty Stadium in November, before losing 2–1 in Cardiff in April after a late <a href="/wiki/Michael_Chopra" title="Michael Chopra">Michael Chopra</a> strike. With Swansea and Cardiff both pushing for promotion to the <a href="/wiki/Premier_League" title="Premier League">Premier League</a>, the first derby at the new <a href="/wiki/Cardiff_City_Stadium" title="Cardiff City Stadium">Cardiff City Stadium</a>, and the first Cardiff win in nine meetings between the sides, was billed as being the biggest South Wales derby of all time, in respect to the league positions of the teams and how close it came to the end of the season. Despite their promising league positions leading up to the derby, neither side gained promotion at the end of that campaign, and so the South Wales derby was once again played out at Championship level during the 2010–11 season – Swansea beating Cardiff 1–0 away with a late winner from then on-loan <a href="/wiki/Marvin_Emnes" title="Marvin Emnes">Marvin Emnes</a> before losing their home game due to a late strike from <a href="/wiki/Craig_Bellamy" title="Craig Bellamy">Craig Bellamy</a>.</p>
<p>Following Swansea's promotion to the Premier League at the end of the 2010–11 season, the South Wales derby was again put on hiatus. It would be two seasons before the sides met once more, this time on the worldwide stage of the Premier League. On 3 November 2013, Cardiff took the bragging rights in the first ever Premier League South Wales derby, enjoying a 1–0 win courtesy of ex-Swan <a href="/wiki/Steven_Caulker" title="Steven Caulker">Steven Caulker</a> at the Cardiff City Stadium. The return fixture for that season took place on 8 February 2014 at Swansea's Liberty Stadium, a match in which interim player-manager Garry Monk would make his managerial debut following the sacking of Michael Laudrup. The Swans took revenge for the defeat earlier in the season with a convincing 3–0 win.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Honours">Honours</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Swansea_City_A.F.C.&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Honours">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:League_Cup_at_Old_Trafford.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1025" data-file-width="935" height="241" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fc/League_Cup_at_Old_Trafford.jpg/220px-League_Cup_at_Old_Trafford.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fc/League_Cup_at_Old_Trafford.jpg/330px-League_Cup_at_Old_Trafford.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fc/League_Cup_at_Old_Trafford.jpg/440px-League_Cup_at_Old_Trafford.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:League_Cup_at_Old_Trafford.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Swansea won the League Cup in 2013, their first major trophy in England.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Swansea City's first trophy was the <a href="/wiki/Welsh_Cup" title="Welsh Cup">Welsh Cup</a>, which they won as Swansea Town in 1913. Their first league honour came in 1925, when they won the 1924–25 <a href="/wiki/Football_League_Third_Division_South" title="Football League Third Division South">Football League Third Division South</a> title. Since then Swansea have gone on to win the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Football_League_Cup" title="Football League Cup">League Cup</a> once, the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Football_League_Trophy" title="Football League Trophy">Football League Trophy</a> twice and the Welsh Cup a further nine times. They have also qualified for <a href="/wiki/UEFA_Cup_Winners%27_Cup" title="UEFA Cup Winners' Cup">UEFA Cup Winners' Cup</a> seven times and the <a href="/wiki/UEFA_Europa_League" title="UEFA Europa League">UEFA Europa League</a> once.</p>
<p>Swansea City's honours include the following:<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-41"><a href="#cite_note-41">[41]</a></sup></p>
<p><b>The Football League</b></p>
<ul>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/List_of_winners_of_English_Football_League_Championship_and_predecessors" title="List of winners of English Football League Championship and predecessors">English second tier</a> (currently <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Football_League_Championship" title="Football League Championship">Football League Championship</a>)
<ul>
<li>Promoted (1): <a href="/wiki/1980%E2%80%9381_in_English_football" title="1980–81 in English football">1980–81</a></li>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Football_League_Championship_play-offs" title="Football League Championship play-offs">Play-off</a> winners (1): <a href="/wiki/2010%E2%80%9311_in_English_football" title="2010–11 in English football">2010–11</a></li>
</ul>
</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/List_of_winners_of_English_Football_League_One_and_predecessors" title="List of winners of English Football League One and predecessors">English third tier</a> (currently <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Football_League_One" title="Football League One">Football League One</a>)
<ul>
<li>Winners (3): <a href="/wiki/1924%E2%80%9325_in_English_football" title="1924–25 in English football">1924–25</a>, <a href="/wiki/1948%E2%80%9349_in_English_football" title="1948–49 in English football">1948–49</a>, <a href="/wiki/2007%E2%80%9308_in_English_football" title="2007–08 in English football">2007–08</a></li>

</ul>
