<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Statistics_and_records">Statistics and records</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Swansea_City_A.F.C.&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Statistics and records">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">For more details on this topic, see <a href="/wiki/List_of_Swansea_City_A.F.C._records_and_statistics" title="List of Swansea City A.F.C. records and statistics">List of Swansea City A.F.C. records and statistics</a>.</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Wilfried_Bony_(2013).JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="499" data-file-width="374" height="294" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f4/Wilfried_Bony_%282013%29.JPG/220px-Wilfried_Bony_%282013%29.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f4/Wilfried_Bony_%282013%29.JPG/330px-Wilfried_Bony_%282013%29.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/f/f4/Wilfried_Bony_%282013%29.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Wilfried_Bony_(2013).JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Wilfried_Bony" title="Wilfried Bony">Wilfried Bony</a> is Swansea's 2nd most expensive signing (£12 million) and most expensive sale (£28 million)</div>
</div>
</div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Wilfred_Milne" title="Wilfred Milne">Wilfred Milne</a> holds the record for Swansea appearances, having played 586 matches between 1920 and 1937, closely followed by <a href="/wiki/Roger_Freestone" title="Roger Freestone">Roger Freestone</a> with 563 between 1991 and 2004.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-42"><a href="#cite_note-42">[42]</a></sup> The player who has won the most international caps while at the club is <a href="/wiki/Ashley_Williams_(footballer)" title="Ashley Williams (footballer)">Ashley Williams</a> with 50 for <a href="/wiki/Wales_national_football_team" title="Wales national football team">Wales</a>.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (April 2014)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<p>The goalscoring record is held by <a href="/wiki/Ivor_Allchurch" title="Ivor Allchurch">Ivor Allchurch</a>, with 166 goals, scored between 1947 and 1958 and between 1965 and 1968.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Rothmans9900_43-0"><a href="#cite_note-Rothmans9900-43">[43]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Cyril_Pearce" title="Cyril Pearce">Cyril Pearce</a> holds the records for the most goals scored in a season, in <a href="/wiki/1931%E2%80%9332_Football_League#Second_Division" title="1931–32 Football League">1931–32</a>, with 35 league goals in the <a href="/wiki/Football_League_Second_Division" title="Football League Second Division">Second Division</a> and 40 goals in total.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ClubHistory_29-1"><a href="#cite_note-ClubHistory-29">[29]</a></sup></p>
<p>The club's widest victory margin in the league was 12–0, a scoreline which they achieved once in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/UEFA_Cup_Winner%27s_Cup" title="UEFA Cup Winner's Cup">European Cup Winners Cup</a>, against <a href="/wiki/Sliema_Wanderers_F.C." title="Sliema Wanderers F.C.">Sliema</a> in 1982.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ClubHistory_29-2"><a href="#cite_note-ClubHistory-29">[29]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-UEFA_Record_44-0"><a href="#cite_note-UEFA_Record-44">[44]</a></sup> They have lost by an eight-goal margin on two occasions, once in the <a href="/wiki/FA_Cup" title="FA Cup">FA Cup</a>, beaten 0–8 by <a href="/wiki/Liverpool_F.C." title="Liverpool F.C.">Liverpool</a> in 1990 and once in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/UEFA_Cup_Winner%27s_Cup" title="UEFA Cup Winner's Cup">European Cup Winners Cup</a>, beaten 0–8 by <a href="/wiki/AS_Monaco_FC" title="AS Monaco FC">AS Monaco</a> in 1991.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SwanseaStattoRecords_45-0"><a href="#cite_note-SwanseaStattoRecords-45">[45]</a></sup></p>
<p>Swansea's home attendance record was set at the fourth-round FA Cup tie against <a href="/wiki/Arsenal_F.C." title="Arsenal F.C.">Arsenal</a> on 17 February 1968, with 32,796 fans attending the <a href="/wiki/Vetch_Field" title="Vetch Field">Vetch Field</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ClubHistory_29-3"><a href="#cite_note-ClubHistory-29">[29]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-46"><a href="#cite_note-46">[46]</a></sup> The most expensive player bought was <a href="/wiki/Borja_Gonz%C3%A1lez" title="Borja González">Borja Bastón</a>, who joined from <a href="/wiki/Atl%C3%A9tico_Madrid" title="Atlético Madrid">Atlético Madrid</a> in August 2016 for a fee of £15 million.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-47"><a href="#cite_note-47">[47]</a></sup> The most expensive sale is <a href="/wiki/Wilfried_Bony" title="Wilfried Bony">Wilfried Bony</a> who joined <a href="/wiki/Manchester_City_F.C." title="Manchester City F.C.">Manchester City</a> in January 2015 for £28 million.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-48"><a href="#cite_note-48">[48]</a></sup></p>

<p>40 <span class="flagicon"><a href="/wiki/Austria" title="Austria"><img alt="Austria" class="thumbborder" data-file-height="600" data-file-width="900" height="15" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/41/Flag_of_Austria.svg/23px-Flag_of_Austria.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/41/Flag_of_Austria.svg/35px-Flag_of_Austria.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/41/Flag_of_Austria.svg/45px-Flag_of_Austria.svg.png 2x" width="23"/></a></span> <a href="/wiki/Besian_Idrizaj" title="Besian Idrizaj">Besian Idrizaj</a> (2009–10) – <i>posthumous</i><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-69"><a href="#cite_note-69">[69]</a></sup></p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Club_officials">Club officials</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Swansea_City_A.F.C.&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Club officials">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p><b>Management</b></p>
<dl>
<dd><i>As of 27 October 2016</i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Whos_Who_70-0"><a href="#cite_note-Whos_Who-70">[70]</a></sup></dd>
</dl>
<p>On the 22 July 2016, Jason Levien and Steve Kaplan led a consortium of American businessmen who bought a 68% stake in the club for £110 million. On the 27 October 2016, Chris Pearlman was appointed the club's first Chief Operating Officer, reporting directly to the chairman and board of directors.</p>
<ul>
<li>Owners: <span class="flagicon"><a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States"><img alt="United States" class="thumbborder" data-file-height="650" data-file-width="1235" height="12" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/a/a4/Flag_of_the_United_States.svg/23px-Flag_of_the_United_States.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/a/a4/Flag_of_the_United_States.svg/35px-Flag_of_the_United_States.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/a/a4/Flag_of_the_United_States.svg/46px-Flag_of_the_United_States.svg.png 2x" width="23"/></a></span> <a href="/wiki/Jason_Levien" title="Jason Levien">Jason Levien</a> and <span class="flagicon"><a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States"><img alt="United States" class="thumbborder" data-file-height="650" data-file-width="1235" height="12" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/a/a4/Flag_of_the_United_States.svg/23px-Flag_of_the_United_States.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/a/a4/Flag_of_the_United_States.svg/35px-Flag_of_the_United_States.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/a/a4/Flag_of_the_United_States.svg/46px-Flag_of_the_United_States.svg.png 2x" width="23"/></a></span> Steve Kaplan</li>
<li>Chairman: <span class="flagicon"><a href="/wiki/Wales" title="Wales"><img alt="Wales" class="thumbborder" data-file-height="498" data-file-width="830" height="14" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/59/Flag_of_Wales_2.svg/23px-Flag_of_Wales_2.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/59/Flag_of_Wales_2.svg/35px-Flag_of_Wales_2.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/59/Flag_of_Wales_2.svg/46px-Flag_of_Wales_2.svg.png 2x" width="23"/></a></span> <a href="/wiki/Huw_Jenkins_(Welsh_businessman)" title="Huw Jenkins (Welsh businessman)">Huw Jenkins</a></li>

<li>Chief Operating Officer: <span class="flagicon"><a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States"><img alt="United States" class="thumbborder" data-file-height="650" data-file-width="1235" height="12" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/a/a4/Flag_of_the_United_States.svg/23px-Flag_of_the_United_States.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/a/a4/Flag_of_the_United_States.svg/35px-Flag_of_the_United_States.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/a/a4/Flag_of_the_United_States.svg/46px-Flag_of_the_United_States.svg.png 2x" width="23"/></a></span> Chris Pearlman</li>
<li>Directors: <span class="flagicon"><a href="/wiki/Wales" title="Wales"><img alt="Wales" class="thumbborder" data-file-height="498" data-file-width="830" height="14" <p><b>Staff</b></p>
<dl>
<dd><i>As of 3 January 2017</i>.</dd>
</dl>
<p>On 27 December 2016, American coach <a href="/wiki/Bob_Bradley" title="Bob Bradley">Bob Bradley</a> was sacked by the club after 11 Premier League matches and a win percentage of just 18.1%. Fitness coach <a href="/wiki/Pierre_Barrieu" title="Pierre Barrieu">Pierre Barrieu</a> and assistant coach <a href="/wiki/Paul_Williams_(footballer,_born_1971)" title="Paul Williams (footballer, born 1971)">Paul Williams</a> also left the club. After a period with <a href="/wiki/Alan_Curtis_(footballer)" title="Alan Curtis (footballer)">Alan Curtis</a> in charge, <a href="/wiki/FC_Bayern_Munich" title="FC Bayern Munich">Bayern Munich</a> assistant manager <a href="/wiki/Paul_Clement_(football_manager)" title="Paul Clement (football manager)">Paul Clement</a> agreed a two-and-a-half year deal to take charge on 3 January 2017.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Clement_28-1"><a href="#cite_note-Clement-28">[28]</a></sup> Following Clement's arrival, <a href="/wiki/Nigel_Gibbs" title="Nigel Gibbs">Nigel Gibbs</a> and <a href="/wiki/Claude_Mak%C3%A9l%C3%A9l%C3%A9" title="Claude Makélélé">Claude Makélélé</a> were appointed his assistant coaches and Karl Halabi was appointed Head of Physical Performance.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-71"><a href="#cite_note-71">[71]</a></sup></p>

</ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Notable_managers">Notable managers</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Swansea_City_A.F.C.&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Notable managers">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/List_of_Swansea_City_A.F.C._managers" title="List of Swansea City A.F.C. managers">List of Swansea City A.F.C. managers</a></div>
<p>There have had thirty-seven permanent managers (of whom six have been player-managers), and four <a href="/wiki/Caretaker_manager" title="Caretaker manager">caretaker managers</a> of Swansea City since the appointment of the club's first professional manager, <a href="/wiki/Walter_Whittaker" title="Walter Whittaker">Walter Whittaker</a> in 1912.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-74"><a href="#cite_note-74">[74]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-75"><a href="#cite_note-75">[75]</a></sup> In the club's first season, Whittaker led Swansea to their first <a href="/wiki/Welsh_Cup" title="Welsh Cup">Welsh Cup</a> win.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ClubHistory_29-4"><a href="#cite_note-ClubHistory-29">[29]</a></sup> The club's longest-serving manager, in terms of tenure, was <a href="/wiki/Haydn_Green" title="Haydn Green">Haydn Green</a>, who held the position for eight years, four months and 14 days, spanning the entirety of <a href="/wiki/World_War_II" title="World War II">World War II</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-76"><a href="#cite_note-76">[76]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Trevor_Morris_(footballer)" title="Trevor Morris (footballer)">Trevor Morris</a>, who oversaw the most number of games at Swansea, was also the first manager to lead a Welsh club in Europe, qualifying for the <a href="/wiki/1961%E2%80%9362_European_Cup_Winners%27_Cup" title="1961–62 European Cup Winners' Cup">1961–62 Cup Winners' Cup</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ClubHistory_29-5"><a href="#cite_note-ClubHistory-29">[29]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-77"><a href="#cite_note-77">[77]</a></sup></p>
<p><a href="/wiki/John_Toshack" title="John Toshack">John Toshack</a>, Swansea City's most successful manager with three league promotions and three <a href="/wiki/Welsh_Cup" title="Welsh Cup">Welsh Cup</a> wins, led the club to their highest league finish, sixth place in the <a href="/wiki/1981%E2%80%9382_in_English_football" title="1981–82 in English football">1981–82</a> <a href="/wiki/Football_League_First_Division" title="Football League First Division">First Division</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ClubHistory_29-6"><a href="#cite_note-ClubHistory-29">[29]</a></sup> Appointed in February 1996, the Dane <a href="/wiki/Jan_M%C3%B8lby" title="Jan Mølby">Jan Mølby</a> became Swansea City's first foreign manager and took Swansea to the 1996–97 <a href="/wiki/Football_League_Third_Division" title="Football League Third Division">Division Three</a> play-off final, only to lose to a last-minute goal.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ClubHistory_29-7"><a href="#cite_note-ClubHistory-29">[29]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-78"><a href="#cite_note-78">[78]</a></sup> In 2011, Swansea City achieved promotion to the <a href="/wiki/Premier_League" title="Premier League">Premier League</a> under <a href="/wiki/Brendan_Rodgers" title="Brendan Rodgers">Brendan Rodgers</a>, becoming the first Welsh team to play in the division since its formation in 1992.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-79"><a href="#cite_note-79">[79]</a></sup> During Swansea City's centenary year (2012–13), the club won the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Football_League_Cup" title="Football League Cup">League Cup</a> for the first time under <a href="/wiki/Michael_Laudrup" title="Michael Laudrup">Michael Laudrup</a>, the first major trophy in Swansea's 100-year history.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-80"><a href="#cite_note-80">[80]</a></sup></p>
